Free palestine
20 years ago, I went in a small village in Armenia to work as a volunteer on an archeological site (I'm French). I had the choice to go to many countries but I made up my mind because I loved (and still love) SOAD so much. It was the most beautiful trip of my life. Despite Armenian's liveliness, I was feeling their pain and the ghosts of the genocide when I would speak to them about it (when it was not too painful to them) and when I would listen to traditional songs, especially the ones played by the master Djivan Gasparyan and his the beautifully haunting duduk melodies.  20 years later on, and still no recognition of the genocide...  SOAD has made so much to pay tribute to their country and make its history largely known to the outer world (even though it should be known without them), while at the same time speaking about their lives in modern America.  The blend between metal and Armenian influences is what makes SOAD, Scars on Broadway or Serj's solo projects such great bands.  Armenia will be in my heart forever, long live Armenia !!â¤ And long live melting-pot societies, at a time when too many countries want to close their frontiers and shut themselves away.

Good lyrics. Bad aransemen music
When I was a kid in Chile, I never missed Titanes del Ring, a wrestling show where my favourite wrestler was Martin Karadagian (1922-1991). In fact, he created the show. He was born in Buenos Aires, to Argentinean mother and Armenian father. He was introduced as "the Armenian Martin Karadagian, the one who drives widows crazy". By this they meant the women who were widowed when he defeated their husbands ("the Mummy", "Pepino the Clown", etc.) in the ring. Sure, it was wrestling, nobody died, but what a show, folks, to see him advance to the ring followed by an entourage of "widows", still weeping.   Therefore, as a child, in Chile, thousands of kilometres from Armenia, I had a pleasant impression of Armenians. So when as an adult I started listening to SOAD, and learned of their Armenian background, in addition to their fantastic music, I viewed them with the same affection as I did with the Martin Karadagian of my childhood. Later on, I went to their Reunion Tour concert in Santiago, Chile, on 7 October 2011. After they opened  with "Prison Song", Serj condemned the atrocities perpetrated back in 1973 by the government of Richard Nixon and his lieutenant Henry Kissinger, in connection with the coup d'Ã©tat that sent Chile back to the middle ages with the murderous dictatorship of Augusto Pinochet. Wow, these men know about genocide and repression, I thought. And solidarity. Their people have felt it in the flesh. Respect and gratitude from Chile!

This hits so close to home right now. Here in Colombia we are currently going through protests due to a ridiculously corrupt tax reform that was the last straw after years of this kind of shit, and unfortunately they have turned violent and bloody, with corpses stacking up each day.  As you can imagine, most of the national news outlets have been noticeably biased in favor of the government while ignoring what is really happening in our streets, but thankfully the people have not stayed quiet and have cought the attention of international media who are on our side for the most part.  I don't usually write these kinds of comments, but your music has always struck a cord with me, and this one in particular feels like it perfectly describes our sentiment even if our situations are not exactly the same, we are angry and frustrated and disappointed, yet unwilling to take this blow without a fight.  If this has peaked your interest I invite you to look up what is happening in Colombia right now. I personally hope that your efforts have helped your cause, and I thank you for helping me put into words the feeling we have towards ours.  #SOSColombia

The paradigm shift I'm trying to bring to light is that you have your natural impulses and you have society itself. It's been covered different angles, but it stems back to how if you want to improve society, tearing it down is not enough. You have to understand what makes different systems work, and understand what needs are to be addressed in order for that social system to evolve. It brings your own power back to yourself, since it forces you to address how you see your own issues are reflected in society/parenthood/social-life or whatever else. Thus changing the world becomes a matter of growing.

It is righteous to come together when the fact you might have personal differences in your relationship as human beings becomes the afterthought, but you realize that your common calling and what you are able to do as a collective could be the right thing to do. That is what I see here. They did not want to make music together anymore - now here they are. Maybe this foreshadows something, maybe they will - beyond this - find a way to look past whatever let them drift apart and they can summon their energy as a band again and their friendship.
